<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Commons-logo.svg"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="1376" data-file-width="1024" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/30px-Commons-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/45px-Commons-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/59px-Commons-logo.svg.png 2x" width="30"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikimedia Commons has media related to <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:2010" title="commons:Category:2010">2010</a></b></i>.</td>

</table>
<p><b>2010 (<a href="/wiki/Roman_numerals" title="Roman numerals">MMX</a>)</b> was a <a href="/wiki/Common_year" title="Common year">common year</a> <a href="/wiki/Common_year_starting_on_Friday" title="Common year starting on Friday">starting on Friday</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dominical_letter" title="Dominical letter">dominical letter</a> C) of the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian calendar</a>, the 2010th year of the <a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">Common Era</a> (CE) and <i><a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">Anno Domini</a></i> (AD) designations, the 10th year of the <a href="/wiki/3rd_millennium" title="3rd millennium">3rd millennium</a>, the 10th year of the <a href="/wiki/21st_century" title="21st century">21st century</a>, and the 1st year of the <a href="/wiki/2010s" title="2010s">2010s</a> decade.</p>
<p>2010 was designated as:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_Year_of_Biodiversity" title="International Year of Biodiversity">International Year of Biodiversity</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_Year_of_Youth" title="International Year of Youth">International Year of Youth</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2010_European_Year_for_Combating_Poverty_and_Social_Exclusion" title="2010 European Year for Combating Poverty and Social Exclusion">2010 European Year for Combating Poverty and Social Exclusion</a></li>
<li>International Year for the Rapprochement of Cultures</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronunciation">Pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Pronunciation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2010s#Pronunciation" title="2010s">2010s § Pronunciation</a></div>
<p>There is a debate among experts and the general public on how to pronounce specific years of the 21st century in English. The year 2010 is pronounced either "two thousand (and) ten", or "twenty-ten".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> 2010 was the first year to have a wide variation in pronunciation, as the <a href="/wiki/2000s_(decade)" title="2000s (decade)">years 2000 to 2009</a> were generally pronounced "two thousand (and) one, two, three, etc." as opposed to the less common "twenty-oh-_".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January">January</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: January">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_Earthquake_building_damage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Haiti_Earthquake_building_damage.jpg/220px-Haiti_Earthquake_building_damage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Haiti_Earthquake_building_damage.jpg/330px-Haiti_Earthquake_building_damage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Haiti_Earthquake_building_damage.jpg/440px-Haiti_Earthquake_building_damage.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_Earthquake_building_damage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damaged buildings in <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a> following the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">Haiti earthquake</a> in January 12.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/January_4" title="January 4">January 4</a> – The tallest man-made structure to date, the <a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">Burj Khalifa</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, is officially opened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAtoday_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAtoday-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opening_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-opening-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-4">[4]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/January_8" title="January 8">January 8</a> – The <a href="/wiki/Togo_national_football_team" title="Togo national football team">Togo national football team</a> is involved in <a href="/wiki/Togo_national_football_team_attack" title="Togo national football team attack">an attack</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, and as a result withdraws from the <a href="/wiki/2010_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2010 Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a>. The attack was perpetrated by the <a href="/wiki/Front_for_the_Liberation_of_the_Enclave_of_Cabinda" title="Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda">FLEC</a>, their first since the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/January_12" title="January 12">January 12</a> – A <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">7.0-magnitude earthquake</a> occurs in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, devastating the nation's capital, <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a>. With a confirmed death toll over 316,000,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MiamiHerald13_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-MiamiHerald13-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN13_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN13-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> it is the seventh <a href="/wiki/Lists_of_earthquakes#Deadliest_earthquakes_on_record" title="Lists of earthquakes">deadliest on record</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/January_15" title="January 15">January 15</a>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_January_15,_2010" title="Solar eclipse of January 15, 2010">longest annular solar eclipse</a> of the <a href="/wiki/3rd_millennium" title="3rd millennium">3rd millennium</a> occurs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chadian_Civil_War_(2005%E2%80%9310)" title="Chadian Civil War (2005–10)">Chadian Civil War (2005–10)</a> officially ends.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/January_25" title="January 25">January 25</a> – <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Airlines_Flight_409" title="Ethiopian Airlines Flight 409">Ethiopian Airlines Flight 409</a> crashes into the Mediterranean shortly after take-off from <a href="/wiki/Beirut%E2%80%93Rafic_Hariri_International_Airport" title="Beirut–Rafic Hariri International Airport">Beirut–Rafic Hariri International Airport</a>, killing all 90 people on board.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="February">February</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: February">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/February_3" title="February 3">February 3</a> – The sculpture <i><a href="/wiki/L%27Homme_qui_marche_I" title="L'Homme qui marche I">L'Homme qui marche I</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Giacometti" title="Alberto Giacometti">Alberto Giacometti</a> sells in London for <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>65 million (US$103.7 million), setting a new world record for a work of art sold at auction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/February_12" title="February 12">February 12</a>–<a href="/wiki/February_28" title="February 28">28</a> – The <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a> are held in Vancouver and <a href="/wiki/Whistler,_British_Columbia" title="Whistler, British Columbia">Whistler</a>, Canada.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/February_18" title="February 18">February 18</a> – The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_of_Niger" title="President of Niger">President of Niger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mamadou_Tandja" title="Mamadou Tandja">Mamadou Tandja</a>, is overthrown after a group of soldiers <a href="/wiki/2010_Nigerien_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2010 Nigerien coup d'état">storms the presidential palace</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Todd_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Todd-11">[11]</a></sup> and form a ruling junta, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_for_the_Restoration_of_Democracy" title="Supreme Council for the Restoration of Democracy">Supreme Council for the Restoration of Democracy</a> headed by <i><a href="/wiki/Chef_d%27escadron" title="Chef d'escadron">chef d'escadron</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Salou_Djibo" title="Salou Djibo">Salou Djibo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ousts_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ousts-12">[12]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/February_27" title="February 27">February 27</a> – An <a href="/wiki/2010_Chile_earthquake" title="2010 Chile earthquake">8.8-magnitude earthquake</a> occurs in <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, triggering a <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a> over the Pacific and killing at least 525.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-muertos_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-muertos-13">[13]</a></sup> The earthquake is one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_earthquakes_by_magnitude" title="Largest earthquakes by magnitude">largest</a> in recorded history.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="March">March</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: March">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/March_16" title="March 16">March 16</a> – The <a href="/wiki/Kasubi_Tombs" title="Kasubi Tombs">Kasubi Tombs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>'s only cultural <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>, are destroyed by fire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/March_26" title="March 26">March 26</a> – The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ROKS_Cheonan_(PCC-772)" title="ROKS Cheonan (PCC-772)">ROKS Cheonan</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Korea_Navy" title="Republic of Korea Navy">South Korean Navy</a> ship carrying 104 personnel, <a href="/wiki/ROKS_Cheonan_sinking" title="ROKS Cheonan sinking">sinks</a> off the country's west coast, killing 46. In May, an independent investigation blames <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, which denies the allegations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dailynk1_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-dailynk1-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April">April</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: April">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/April_7" title="April 7">April 7</a> – <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyz</a> President <a href="/wiki/Kurmanbek_Bakiyev" title="Kurmanbek Bakiyev">Kurmanbek Bakiyev</a> flees the country amid fierce <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_Revolution_of_2010" title="Kyrgyz Revolution of 2010">anti-government riots</a> in the capital, <a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/April_10" title="April 10">April 10</a> – The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Poland" title="President of Poland">President of Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lech_Kaczy%C5%84ski" title="Lech Kaczyński">Lech Kaczyński</a>, is among 96 killed when their airplane <a href="/wiki/2010_Polish_Air_Force_Tu-154_crash" title="2010 Polish Air Force Tu-154 crash">crashes</a> near <a href="/wiki/Smolensk" title="Smolensk">Smolensk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/April_14" title="April 14">April 14</a> – <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash" title="Volcanic ash">Volcanic ash</a> from one of <a href="/wiki/2010_eruptions_of_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="2010 eruptions of Eyjafjallajökull">several eruptions</a> beneath Mount <a href="/wiki/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="Eyjafjallajökull">Eyjafjallajökull</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Ice_cap" title="Ice cap">ice cap</a> in <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, begins to <a href="/wiki/Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption" title="Air travel disruption after the 2010 Eyjafjallajökull eruption">disrupt air traffic</a> across northern and western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASInfo_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASInfo-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC8622438_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC8622438-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/April_20" title="April 20">April 20</a> – The <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_explosion" title="Deepwater Horizon explosion">Deepwater Horizon oil drilling platform explodes</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, killing 11 workers. The resulting <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill" title="Deepwater Horizon oil spill">Horizon oil spill</a>, one of the largest in history, spreads for several months, damaging the waters and the United States coastline, and prompting international debate and doubt about the practice and procedures of <a href="/wiki/Offshore_drilling" title="Offshore drilling">offshore drilling</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wardell_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wardell-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/April_27" title="April 27">April 27</a> – <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">Standard &amp; Poor's</a> <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Greece#2010_debt_crisis" title="Economy of Greece">downgrades</a> Greece's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sovereign_rating" title="Sovereign rating">sovereign credit</a> rating to <a href="/wiki/High-yield_debt" title="High-yield debt">junk</a> 4 days after the activation of a <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>45-billion <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>–<a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a> bailout, triggering the decline of <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock markets</a> worldwide and of the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>'s value,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_2_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-27">[27]</a></sup> and furthering a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_European_sovereign_debt_crisis" title="2010 European sovereign debt crisis">European sovereign debt crisis</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="May">May</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: May">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/May_2" title="May 2">May 2</a> – The <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> agree to a €110 billion bailout package for Greece. The package involves sharp Greek <a href="/wiki/Austerity" title="Austerity">austerity</a> measures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/May_4" title="May 4">May 4</a> – <i><a href="/wiki/Nude,_Green_Leaves_and_Bust" title="Nude, Green Leaves and Bust">Nude, Green Leaves and Bust</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Pablo Picasso</a> sells in New York for <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>106.5 million, setting another new world record for a work of art sold at auction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/May_6" title="May 6">May 6</a> – The <a href="/wiki/2010_Flash_Crash" title="2010 Flash Crash">2010 Flash Crash</a>, a trillion-dollar stock market crash, occurs over 36 minutes, initiated by a series of automated trading programs in a feedback loop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phillips-5-11-10_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-phillips-5-11-10-32">[32]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/May_7" title="May 7">May 7</a>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> becomes the 31st member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li>Scientists conducting the <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal_genome_project" title="Neanderthal genome project">Neanderthal genome project</a> announce that they have <a href="/wiki/DNA_sequencing" title="DNA sequencing">sequenced</a> enough of the <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a> <a href="/wiki/Genome" title="Genome">genome</a> to suggest that Neanderthals and humans may have <a href="/wiki/Archaic_human_admixture_with_modern_humans" title="Archaic human admixture with modern humans">interbred</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pinkowski_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pinkowski-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Green_Krause_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Green_Krause-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/May_12" title="May 12">May 12</a> – <a href="/wiki/Afriqiyah_Airways_Flight_771" title="Afriqiyah Airways Flight 771">Afriqiyah Airways Flight 771</a> crashes at runway at <a href="/wiki/Tripoli_International_Airport" title="Tripoli International Airport">Tripoli International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, killing 103 of the 104 people on board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/May_19" title="May 19">May 19</a> – <a href="/wiki/2010_Thai_political_protests" title="2010 Thai political protests">Protests</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, end with a bloody military crackdown, killing 91 and injuring more than 2,100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deaths_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-deaths-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/May_20" title="May 20">May 20</a>
<ul>
<li>Scientists announced that they have created a functional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gene_synthesis#Entire_genomes" title="Gene synthesis">synthetic genome</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li>Five paintings worth €100 million are stolen from the <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_d%27Art_Moderne_de_la_Ville_de_Paris" title="Musée d'Art Moderne de la Ville de Paris">Musée d'Art Moderne de la Ville de Paris</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sky_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-sky-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/May_22" title="May 22">May 22</a> – <a href="/wiki/Air_India_Express_Flight_812" title="Air India Express Flight 812">Air India Express Flight 812</a> overshoots the runway at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mangalore_Airport_(India)" title="Mangalore Airport (India)">Mangalore International Airport</a> in India, killing 158 and leaving 8 survivors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/May_31" title="May 31">May 31</a> – Nine activists are <a href="/wiki/Gaza_flotilla_raid" title="Gaza flotilla raid">killed in a clash</a> with soldiers when Israeli Navy forces raid and capture a flotilla of ships attempting to break the <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Blockade of the Gaza Strip">Gaza blockade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edition.cnn.com_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-edition.cnn.com-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="June">June</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: June">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/June_10" title="June 10">June 10</a>–<a href="/wiki/June_14" title="June 14">14</a> – <a href="/wiki/2010_South_Kyrgyzstan_ethnic_clashes" title="2010 South Kyrgyzstan ethnic clashes">Ethnic riots</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a> between <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_people" title="Kyrgyz people">Kyrgyz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a> result in the deaths of hundreds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/June_11" title="June 11">June 11</a> – <a href="/wiki/July_11" title="July 11">July 11</a> – The <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a> is held in South Africa, and is won by <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a>, with the runner-up being the Netherlands.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="July">July</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: July">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/July_8" title="July 8">July 8</a> – The first 24-hour flight by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar-powered_plane" title="Solar-powered plane">solar-powered plane</a> is completed by the <a href="/wiki/Solar_Impulse" title="Solar Impulse">Solar Impulse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/July_21" title="July 21">July 21</a> – <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> becomes the 32nd member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/July_25" title="July 25">July 25</a> – <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a>, an online publisher of anonymous, covert, and classified material, leaks to the public <a href="/wiki/Afghan_War_documents_leak" title="Afghan War documents leak">over 90,000 internal reports</a> about the United States-led involvement in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">War in Afghanistan</a> from 2004 to 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/July_29" title="July 29">July 29</a> – Heavy monsoon rains begin to cause <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_Khyber_Pakhtunkhwa_floods" title="2010 Khyber Pakhtunkhwa floods">widespread flooding</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Khyber_Pakhtunkhwa" title="Khyber Pakhtunkhwa">Khyber Pakhtunkhwa</a> province of Pakistan. Over 1,600 are killed, and more than one million are displaced by the floods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="August">August</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: August">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/August_10" title="August 10">August 10</a> – The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> declares the <a href="/wiki/2009_flu_pandemic" title="2009 flu pandemic">H1N1 influenza pandemic</a> over, saying worldwide flu activity has returned to typical seasonal patterns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="September">September</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: September">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/September_4" title="September 4">September 4</a> – A <a href="/wiki/2010_Canterbury_earthquake" title="2010 Canterbury earthquake">7.1 magnitude</a> earthquake rocks <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">Christchurch</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> causing large amounts of damage but no direct fatalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> It is the first in a series of earthquakes between 2010 and 2012 that resulted in the deaths of 187 people and over $40 billion worth of damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Seismologists noted that the earthquake sequence was highly unusual, and likely to never happen again anywhere else in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/September_7" title="September 7">September 7</a> – <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> becomes the 33rd member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October">October</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: October">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/October_10" title="October 10">October 10</a> – The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a> are <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Netherlands_Antilles" title="Dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles">dissolved</a>, with the islands being split up and given a new constitutional status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-time-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/October_22" title="October 22">October 22</a> – The <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> surpasses the <a href="/wiki/List_of_spaceflight_records" title="List of spaceflight records">record</a> for the longest continuous human occupation of space, having been continuously inhabited since November 2, 2000 (3641 days).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/October_23" title="October 23">October 23</a> – In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_G-20_Seoul_summit_preparations" title="2010 G-20 Seoul summit preparations">preparation for the Seoul summit</a>, finance ministers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" title="G-20 major economies">G-20</a> agree to reform the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and shift 6% of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund#Members.27_quotas_and_voting_power.2C_and_board_of_governors" title="International Monetary Fund">voting shares</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_nations" title="Developing nations">developing nations</a> and countries with <a href="/wiki/Emerging_markets" title="Emerging markets">emerging markets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-G20_summit_agrees_to_reform_IMF_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-G20_summit_agrees_to_reform_IMF-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/October_25" title="October 25">October 25</a> – An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/October_2010_Sumatra_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="October 2010 Sumatra earthquake and tsunami">earthquake and consequent tsunami</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, kills over 400 people and leaves hundreds missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_Major_earthquake_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_Major_earthquake-60">[60]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/October_26" title="October 26">October 26</a> – <a href="/wiki/2010_eruptions_of_Mount_Merapi" title="2010 eruptions of Mount Merapi">Repeated eruptions</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Merapi" title="Mount Merapi">Mount Merapi</a> volcano in <a href="/wiki/Central_Java" title="Central Java">Central Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, and accompanying <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_flow" title="Pyroclastic flow">pyroclastic flows</a> of scalding gas, pumice, and <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash" title="Volcanic ash">volcanic ash</a> descending the erupting volcano kill 300 people and force hundreds of thousands of residents to evacuate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_toll_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_toll-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bknpb1_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-bknpb1-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November">November</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: November">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/November_4" title="November 4">November 4</a> – <a href="/wiki/Aero_Caribbean_Flight_883" title="Aero Caribbean Flight 883">Aero Caribbean Flight 883</a> crashes in central <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, killing all 68 people on board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_1106_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_1106-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/November_11" title="November 11">November 11</a>–<a href="/wiki/November_12" title="November 12">12</a> – The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_G-20_Seoul_summit" title="2010 G-20 Seoul summit">G-20 summit</a> is held in <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, South Korea. Korea becomes the first non-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a> nation to host a G-20 leaders summit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/November_13" title="November 13">November 13</a> – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burmese</a> opposition politician <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> is released from her <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">house arrest</a> after being incarcerated since <a href="/wiki/1989" title="1989">1989</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/November_17" title="November 17">November 17</a> – Researchers at <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a> trap 38 <a href="/wiki/Antihydrogen" title="Antihydrogen">antihydrogen</a> <a href="/wiki/Atom" title="Atom">atoms</a> for a sixth of a second, marking the first time in history that humans have trapped <a href="/wiki/Antimatter" title="Antimatter">antimatter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/November_20" title="November 20">November 20</a> – Participants of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Lisbon_summit" title="2010 Lisbon summit">2010 NATO Lisbon summit</a> issue the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Lisbon_Summit_Declaration" title="NATO Lisbon Summit Declaration">Lisbon Summit Declaration</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/November_21" title="November 21">November 21</a> – <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> countries agree to a <a href="/wiki/Post-2008_Irish_economic_downturn#EU-IMF_intervention" title="Post-2008 Irish economic downturn">rescue package</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> from the <a href="/wiki/European_Financial_Stability_Facility" title="European Financial Stability Facility">European Financial Stability Facility</a> in response to the country's <a href="/wiki/Post-2008_Irish_economic_downturn" title="Post-2008 Irish economic downturn">financial crisis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RTE_21.2F11_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-RTE_21.2F11-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/November_23" title="November 23">November 23</a> – <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Yeonpyeong" title="Bombardment of Yeonpyeong">shells</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yeonpyeong_Island" title="Yeonpyeong Island">Yeonpyeong Island</a>, prompting a military response by South Korea. The incident causes an escalation of tension on the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a> and prompts widespread international condemnation. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> declares it to be one of the most serious incidents since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/November_28" title="November 28">November 28</a> – <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a> releases a collection of more than 250,000 American <a href="/wiki/United_States_diplomatic_cables_leak" title="United States diplomatic cables leak">diplomatic cables</a>, including 100,000 <a href="/wiki/Classified_information_in_the_United_States" title="Classified information in the United States">marked "secret" or "confidential"</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manila_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-manila-75">[75]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/November_29" title="November 29">November 29</a> – The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> agree to an €85 billion <a href="/wiki/Bailout" title="Bailout">rescue deal</a> for Ireland from the <a href="/wiki/European_Financial_Stability_Facility" title="European Financial Stability Facility">European Financial Stability Facility</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and bilateral loans from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rescuedeal_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-rescuedeal-76">[76]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/November_29" title="November 29">November 29</a> – <a href="/wiki/December_10" title="December 10">December 10</a> – The <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="2010 United Nations Climate Change Conference">2010 United Nations Climate Change Conference</a> is held in <a href="/wiki/Canc%C3%BAn" title="Cancún">Cancún</a>, Mexico. Also referred to as the 16th Conference of the Parties of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change</a> (COP 16), it serves too as the 6th meeting of the Parties to the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> (CMP 6).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="December">December</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: December">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_9" title="December 9">December 9</a> – <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a> becomes the 34th member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_17" title="December 17">December 17</a> – The attempted <a href="/wiki/Suicide_of_Mohamed_Bouazizi" title="Suicide of Mohamed Bouazizi">suicide of Mohamed Bouazizi</a>, a street vendor in <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, triggers the <a href="/wiki/Tunisian_Revolution" title="Tunisian Revolution">Tunisian Revolution</a> and the wider <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a> throughout the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_21" title="December 21">December 21</a> – The first <a href="/wiki/December_2010_lunar_eclipse" title="December 2010 lunar eclipse">total lunar eclipse</a> to occur on the day of the Northern <a href="/wiki/Winter_solstice" title="Winter solstice">winter solstice</a> and Southern <a href="/wiki/Summer_solstice" title="Summer solstice">summer solstice</a> since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_17th_century_lunar_eclipses" title="List of 17th century lunar eclipses">1638</a> takes place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sir_Ellis_Clarke.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3888" data-file-width="2592" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Sir_Ellis_Clarke.jpg/120px-Sir_Ellis_Clarke.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Sir_Ellis_Clarke.jpg/180px-Sir_Ellis_Clarke.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Sir_Ellis_Clarke.jpg/240px-Sir_Ellis_Clarke.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a>

<a href="/wiki/Ellis_Clarke" title="Ellis Clarke">Ellis Clarke</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_10" title="December 10">December 10</a> – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_B._Fenn" title="John B. Fenn">John B. Fenn</a>, American Nobel chemist (b. <a href="/wiki/1917" title="1917">1917</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_12" title="December 12">December 12</a> – <a href="/wiki/Tom_Walkinshaw" title="Tom Walkinshaw">Tom Walkinshaw</a>, British racing car driver and team owner (b. <a href="/wiki/1946" title="1946">1946</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_13" title="December 13">December 13</a> – <a href="/wiki/Richard_Holbrooke" title="Richard Holbrooke">Richard Holbrooke</a>, American diplomat (b. <a href="/wiki/1941" title="1941">1941</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_15" title="December 15">December 15</a> – <a href="/wiki/Blake_Edwards" title="Blake Edwards">Blake Edwards</a>, American film director (b. <a href="/wiki/1922" title="1922">1922</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_17" title="December 17">December 17</a> – <a href="/wiki/Captain_Beefheart" title="Captain Beefheart">Captain Beefheart</a>, American musician (b. <a href="/wiki/1941" title="1941">1941</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_21" title="December 21">December 21</a> – <a href="/wiki/Enzo_Bearzot" title="Enzo Bearzot">Enzo Bearzot</a>, Italian footballer and coach (b. <a href="/wiki/1927" title="1927">1927</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_25" title="December 25">December 25</a> – <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Andr%C3%A9s_P%C3%A9rez" title="Carlos Andrés Pérez">Carlos Andrés Pérez</a>, 55th President of Venezuela (b. <a href="/wiki/1922" title="1922">1922</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_26" title="December 26">December 26</a>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Salvador_Jorge_Blanco" title="Salvador Jorge Blanco">Salvador Jorge Blanco</a>, 48th President of the Dominican Republic (b. <a href="/wiki/1926" title="1926">1926</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Teena_Marie" title="Teena Marie">Teena Marie</a>, American singer-songwriter (b. <a href="/wiki/1956" title="1956">1956</a>)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_30" title="December 30">December 30</a>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ellis_Clarke" title="Ellis Clarke">Ellis Clarke</a>, 1st President of Trinidad and Tobago (b. <a href="/wiki/1917" title="1917">1917</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bobby_Farrell" title="Bobby Farrell">Bobby Farrell</a>, West Indian-born Dutch dancer (<a href="/wiki/Boney_M." title="Boney M.">Boney M.</a>) (b. <a href="/wiki/1949" title="1949">1949</a>)</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_Prizes">Nobel Prizes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Nobel Prizes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nobel_medal.png"><img alt="Nobel medal.png" data-file-height="1013" data-file-width="1013" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6a/Nobel_medal.png/100px-Nobel_medal.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6a/Nobel_medal.png/150px-Nobel_medal.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6a/Nobel_medal.png/200px-Nobel_medal.png 2x" width="100"/></a></div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Chemistry</a> – <a href="/wiki/Richard_F._Heck" title="Richard F. Heck">Richard F. Heck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ei-ichi_Negishi" title="Ei-ichi Negishi">Ei-ichi Negishi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Akira_Suzuki_(chemist)" title="Akira Suzuki (chemist)">Akira Suzuki</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Economics</a> – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_A._Diamond" title="Peter A. Diamond">Peter A. Diamond</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dale_T._Mortensen" title="Dale T. Mortensen">Dale T. Mortensen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christopher_A._Pissarides" title="Christopher A. Pissarides">Christopher A. Pissarides</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Literature</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mario_Vargas_Llosa" title="Mario Vargas Llosa">Mario Vargas Llosa</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Peace</a> – <a href="/wiki/Liu_Xiaobo" title="Liu Xiaobo">Liu Xiaobo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Physics</a> – <a href="/wiki/Andre_Geim" title="Andre Geim">Andre Geim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Novoselov" title="Konstantin Novoselov">Konstantin Novoselov</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Physiology or Medicine</a> – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_G._Edwards" title="Robert G. Edwards">Robert G. Edwards</a></li>
</ul>
